بموجب حتى يكون فيضه عاماً، والتخصيص بحسب الشرائط ورفع الموانع، فافهم فإنه مما خفي على أقوام . قوله : ( إنما هو بالنسبة إلى تحققهما أي كلياً كما هو مقصود المستدل . قوله : ( في الهويات) أي الأفراد لم يقل في الخارج ليشمل العام والخاص اللذين من الأمور الذهنية كالكيفيات النفسانية. في الاستدلال وبالعكس ، فيدور لأنا نمنع توقف العلم بالأعرفية على العلم بالبداهة على أنه وجه غير ما ذكره الشارح إلا أن يريد التوقف بحسب العلم فتأمل . الأ. قوله : ( في الاستدلال على ذلك ثالثاً قد نبهناك سابقاً على أن هذا القول علة ثانية لأعرفية دعم لا علة ثالثة لأعرفية الوجود كما زعمه الشارح فيما يستفاد من ظاهر كلامه فتأمل . قوله : (قلنا مبني على الموجب بالذات يعني أن مراد المستدل وهو إثبات أعرفية العام إنما يتم في الموجب بالذات، وإلا فيجوز أن يختار المختار، فيض العلم بالخاص ولا يختار فيض العلم بالعام فالقول بأنه ليس مبنياً على الموجب لوجوب الفيض عن المختار أيضاً بعد ارتفاع الموانع وتحقق جميع الشرائط التي من جملتها تعلق إرادته عدول عن محصول الكلام . قوله : ( إنما يعرض للشيء باعتبار ذلك أي التحقق في الهويات وأما بالنسبة إلى التحقق الذهني فلا عموم ولا خصوص، إلا إذا كان المركب معقولاَ بالكنه فالحصر بالنسبة إلى الإطلاق وبهذا يندفع ما يورد على قوله إذ لا علاقة بين الصورتين الذهنيتين من أنه يشكل بالإضافيات والجزء مع الكل، وذلك لأن المراد بالصورتين صورتا الشيئين مطلقاً مثل صورة الإنسان وصورة الحيوان، سواء أخذا بالكنه أو بالوجه وليس القصد إلى خصوصيات الصور.
(The first observatory - the first objective: On defining existence and non-existence) Other than it? (The general is part of the specific is denied, rather the general may be an accidental universal (عرض عام) for the specific, so it is not necessary that from the conception of the specific, even if by essence, the conception of the general follows. Thus the case may be similar for existence.) (His saying) in the third inference on that: (The emanation is general. We said: It is based on the necessitating cause (الموجب بالذات) such that emanation must occur from it when conditions are met and obstacles are removed. But we do not hold that. Rather, all events according to us are attributed to the free agent (الفاعل المختار). So it is possible that knowledge of the specific exists without knowledge of the general.) (And His saying) in this inference: (The conditions and obstacles of the general are fewer than those of the specific.) (We said: That) which you mentioned is only (in relation to their realization) i.e., the realization of the general and specific (in individuals (الهويات)) since generality and particularity only occur to a thing in that respect. So the general is realized in more individuals, and the specific in fewer. So if things are arranged in generality and particularity, like substance relative to the species of man, even its kind, then every condition for the realization of the general or obstacle to it is a condition for the realization of the specific, or? His saying: (We said: Based on the necessitating cause) Its summary: We do not accept the generality of emanation, for He, exalted, is a free agent. It is possible that He emanates the conception of the specific and does not emanate the conception of the general. He is not a necessitator such that His emanation is general. Specification is according to conditions and removal of obstacles. So understand, for it is something that has been hidden from many people. His saying: (It is only in relation to their realization) i.e., universally, as the arguer intended. His saying: (In individuals) i.e., instances; he did not say 'in the external' to include the general and specific that are mental things like psychological qualities. In the inference and conversely, thus it circulates, because we deny that knowledge of the better known depends on knowledge of self-evidence, unless he intends dependence in terms of knowledge, so reflect. The. His saying: (In the third inference on that) We have previously alerted you that this statement is a second cause for the better known? Not a third cause for the better known of existence as the commentator claimed from the apparent meaning of his words, so reflect. His saying: (We said: Based on the necessitating cause) He means that the arguer's intention, which is to prove that the general is better known, only holds in the case of the necessitating cause. Otherwise, the chooser may choose to emanate knowledge of the specific and not choose to emanate knowledge of the general. So the statement that it is not based on the necessitator because emanation from the chooser is also necessary after obstacles are removed and all conditions are met, including the attachment of His will, is a deviation from the gist of the discussion. His saying: (It only occurs to the thing in that respect) i.e., realization in individuals. As for mental realization, there is no generality or particularity, unless the composite is intellectually known by essence, and then the restriction is relative to absoluteness. By this is refuted what is objected to his saying that there is no relation between the two mental images, that it is problematic with relatives and the part with the whole. Because what is meant by the two images is the images of two things absolutely, like the image of man and the image of animal, whether taken by essence or by aspect, and the intention is not to particularities of images.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a commentary refuting the argument that general concepts are better known (أعرف) than specific ones. The commentator addresses three main points. First, he denies that the general is always part of the specific; rather, the general can be an accidental universal (عرض عام) for the specific, so conceiving the specific does not necessarily entail conceiving the general. Second, he responds to the argument that emanation (الفيض) is general by stating that this argument assumes a necessitating cause (الموجب بالذات) where emanation must occur when conditions are met. However, the Ash'ari position is that God is a free agent (الفاعل المختار), so He may choose to create knowledge of the specific without creating knowledge of the general. Third, he discusses the argument that the general has fewer conditions and obstacles than the specific. The commentator replies that this is only true regarding realization in individuals (الهويات), not in mental existence. In mental existence, generality and particularity are not inherent. The commentator further clarifies that the arguer's intention to prove the general is better known only works under the necessitating cause paradigm; with a free agent, God may not create the general knowledge. He also addresses a possible objection about the relationship between two mental images, saying that the images are taken absolutely, not with particular details, so the problems of relatives and part-whole do not arise. The passage ends with a note that the third inference is actually a second cause for the better known, not a third, and warns the reader to reflect carefully.

Key Terms
الهويات
التحقق
العموم
الخصوص
التصور الذهني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The general is always easier to know because it has fewer conditions.
Correction: This only applies to external individuals, not to mental conception; the general may not be mentally simpler.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, the argument that the general has fewer conditions applies to what?
A) Mental conception only.
B) Realization in individuals only.
C) Both external and mental equally.
D) Neither external nor mental.

Key Takeaway
The claim that the general has fewer conditions only holds for external individuals, not for mental conception, so it does not prove the general is better known.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn a general principle, do you assume you have fully understood it, or do you check how it applies to specific cases? Think of a time when your general knowledge failed you in a real situation. How will you test your understanding of important concepts from now on?
?
This lesson shows that what seems true in the mind may not hold in external reality. Where in your own life have you confused a mental assumption with reality? What step will you take today to align your inner beliefs with the external truth?
?
The passage warns against mistaking accidental relationships for essential ones. Consider a belief you hold about yourself that you have never questioned. Is it based on external reality or a mental habit? Ask Allah to show you the truth and commit to seeking evidence.

Second Proof: Existence Cannot Be Superadded
Al-Jurjani argues from the principle that positive attributes require existent subjects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that existence cannot be a superadded attribute because it would require the quiddity to have an existence prior to itself.

Core Idea
Existence cannot be added to quiddity without absurd circularity.

Al-Jurjani presents a concise logical proof that existence is not a superadded attribute. The argument hinges on the principle that any positive attribute requires its subject to be already existent. If existence itself were an attribute, the quiddity would need prior existence, leading to infinite regress or duplication.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the compact argument structure.
The passage includes the matn (few words) and the commentator's expansion.
2
Trace the logical steps
Identify each premise: positive attributes need existent subjects; assume existence is superadded; it would subsist in quiddity; subsistence requires quiddity to exist; therefore circularity or regress.
Focus on the conditional chain: if existence is superadded, then absurdities follow.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why this argument refutes the idea that existence is an accidental attribute. Ask yourself: what would happen if we denied the premise?
The conclusion is that existence is not superadded in any quiddity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني قيام الصفة الثبوتية بالشيء فرع وجوده ) أي وجود ذلك الشيء ( في نفسه ضرورة) فإن ما لا ثبوت له في نفسه لم يمكن أن يتصف بصفة ثبوتية ولا شك أن الوجود أمر ثبوتي ( فلو كان الوجود صفة زائدة [؟] قوله : ( الثاني قيام إلخ) تقريره أنه لو كان الوجود زائداً على ماهية ما لكان قائماً بها، وإذا كان قائماً بها لكان فرعاً على وجودها في نفسها، وإذا كان فرعاً لوجودها في نفسها كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها ينتج لو كان الوجود زائداً على الماهية كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها والتالي باطل لأنه يلزم كون الشيء موجوداً مرتين وتقدم الوجود على نفسه أو التسلسل فكذا المقدم فثبت أن الوجود ليس زائدا في شيء من الماهيات . قوله : ( فإن مالا ثبوت له إلخ إذا المعدوم مسلوب عنه كل صفة وقيد بالثبوتية إذ يتصف المعدوم بالصفات العدمية فإنه في الحقيقة سلب الاتصاف بالصفات الثبوتية، قيل : هذا البيان إنما يدل على الاستلزام دون الفرعية ،والتوقف فالحق أن ثبوت شيء لشيء يستلزم ثبوت المثبت له في طرف الثبوت وحينئذ لا إشكال في قيام الوجود بالماهية والاتصاف به، وعندي أن الانصاف نسبة بين الطرفين فيحتاج إلى ثبوتهما فيه فيكون الاتصاف متوقفاً وفرعاً لثبوت المثبت له، فإن قيل : فيلزم أن يكون فرع ثبوت المثبت أيضاً ، قلت : نعم إذا كان الاتصاف حقيقياً كالاتصاف بالأعراض كما نص عليه الشيخ حيث قال في إلهيات الشفاء : إن ما لا يكون موجوداً في نفسه، استحال أن يكون موجداً لشيء، وأما إذا كان الاتصاف انتزاعياً كاتصاف زيد بالعمى، فلا يقتضي إلا ثبوت المثبت له لأنه لا بد من مبدأ الانتزاع في طرف الاتصاف حتى ينتزع منه.
The second aspect: The subsistence of a positive attribute in a thing is a branch of its existence—i.e., the existence of that thing in itself necessarily. For that which has no subsistence in itself cannot be qualified by a positive attribute, and there is no doubt that existence is a positive thing. So if existence were a superadded attribute [؟]. His statement: 'The second aspect, etc.' Its explanation: If existence were superadded to some quiddity, it would subsist in it; if it subsists in it, it would be a branch of its existence in itself; if it is a branch of its existence in itself, the quiddity would have an existence before its existence. The conclusion: If existence were superadded to the quiddity, the quiddity would have an existence before its existence, and the consequent is false, because it would necessitate the thing being existent twice, and the priority of existence over itself, or infinite regress. So the antecedent is false, thus it is established that existence is not superadded in any quiddity. His statement: 'For that which has no subsistence, etc.' The non-existent is stripped of every attribute, and he restricted it to positive attributes because the non-existent is qualified by privative attributes, for that is actually a negation of qualification by positive attributes. It is said: This demonstration only indicates the implication, not the branch-status and dependence. The truth is that the subsistence of a thing for a thing necessitates the subsistence of the subject of attribution in the realm of subsistence, and then there is no problem in the subsistence of existence in the quiddity and being qualified by it. In my view, attribution is a relation between two sides, so it needs their subsistence in it; thus the qualification is dependent and a branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution. If it is said: Then it would be a branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution as well. I say: Yes, if the attribution is real, like the attribution of accidents, as the Master stated in the Ilāhiyyāt of al-Shifā': 'That which is not existent in itself cannot be the cause of something.' But if the attribution is abstractive, like the attribution of Zayd with blindness, it only requires the subsistence of the subject of attribution, because there must be a principle of abstraction in the side of the attribute from which it is abstracted.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof that existence cannot be a superadded attribute to quiddity. The argument is: A positive attribute (like existence) can only subsist in something that already exists in itself. If existence were a superadded attribute, it would have to subsist in the quiddity. But for it to subsist in the quiddity, the quiddity must already have existence in itself (since the subject of a positive attribute must be existent). This leads to a vicious regress or circularity: the quiddity would need an existence before its own existence. Therefore, existence cannot be superadded; it must be identical to or part of the quiddity. The commentary then discusses a subtlety: the argument might only prove that the quiddity must exist in some respect (thubūt) for the attribute to subsist, not necessarily that it has existence in the same sense. The commentator distinguishes between real attribution (like accidents) where the subject must be existent, and abstractive attribution (like blindness) where only the subject's subsistence in the mind is needed. However, in the case of existence, the attribution is real, so the quiddity must exist in itself before receiving existence as an attribute, which is impossible.

Key Terms
صفة ثبوتية
فرع وجود
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof seems to show that no attribute can be accidental, but that is not the case.
Correction: The proof only targets existence as an attribute, not all attributes. The commentator later distinguishes real vs abstractive attributes.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the second proof regarding existence?
A) Existence is a superadded accident like blackness
B) Existence cannot be superadded because it would require the quiddity to exist before its own existence
C) Existence is identical to the quiddity in all cases
D) Existence is a privative attribute

Key Takeaway
The second proof refutes the superadditiveness of existence by showing it leads to an infinite regress or circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that your existence is not something added to 'you'—you do not possess existence as a property. If your very being is not your own, but is given to you at every moment by Allah, how should that change the way you view your life, your possessions, and your plans? What one concrete step can you take today to live out of that truth?
?
The argument leads to an absurdity if we think we have an independent existence prior to our existence. In your heart, do you sometimes feel as if your identity or your 'self' exists independently of Allah’s constant giving of existence? What would it look like to truly believe that you are nothing without His sustaining presence? Commit to a specific reminder (e.g., a dhikr or reflection) that you will use daily this week.
?
If existence were superadded, it would lead to an infinite regress. But in your daily life, you may act as if your worth or identity depends on a chain of achievements or validations from others, never feeling truly 'existent' enough. How does the logical necessity that existence is foundational challenge this pattern? What would it mean for you to rest in the fact that Allah has given you existence and that is enough? What one attachment or approval can you release to Him today?

Real vs. Abstractive Attribution in the Argument
Commentator distinguishes real vs abstractive attribution to defend the second proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between real and abstractive attribution, and how it clarifies that the second proof only applies to real attributes.

Core Idea
Real attribution requires existence; abstractive attribution does not.

After presenting the second proof, the commentator addresses a potential objection: the argument only shows a conditional implication, not that existence is a branch of quiddity. The response introduces a crucial distinction between real and abstractive attribution. This distinction helps limit the proof's scope and shows why the argument is sound for existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage from 'قوله : ( فإن مالا ثبوت له إلخ' to the end. Understand the objection that the proof only shows implication, not dependence.
The objection is that the argument proves that if existence is superadded, the quiddity must exist, but that is just conditional, not that existence depends on prior existence.
2
Understand the commentator's reply
The commentator clarifies that real attribution (like accidents) requires the subject to be existent, but abstractive attribution (like blindness) only requires mental subsistence. For existence, the attribution is real, so the quiddity must exist in itself.
This reply shows why the proof is valid: existence is a real attribute, so it needs a real subject.
3
Apply the distinction
Consider how this distinction affects the proof. It narrows the conclusion to real attributes; abstractive attributes are not affected. This also addresses the worry that the proof would deny all accidental attributes.
The master's quote from al-Shifa' supports the principle for real attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( الثاني قيام الصفة الثبوتية بالشيء فرع وجوده ) أي وجود ذلك الشيء ( في نفسه ضرورة) فإن ما لا ثبوت له في نفسه لم يمكن أن يتصف بصفة ثبوتية ولا شك أن الوجود أمر ثبوتي ( فلو كان الوجود صفة زائدة [؟] قوله : ( الثاني قيام إلخ) تقريره أنه لو كان الوجود زائداً على ماهية ما لكان قائماً بها، وإذا كان قائماً بها لكان فرعاً على وجودها في نفسها، وإذا كان فرعاً لوجودها في نفسها كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها ينتج لو كان الوجود زائداً على الماهية كان للماهية وجود قبل وجودها والتالي باطل لأنه يلزم كون الشيء موجوداً مرتين وتقدم الوجود على نفسه أو التسلسل فكذا المقدم فثبت أن الوجود ليس زائدا في شيء من الماهيات . قوله : ( فإن مالا ثبوت له إلخ إذا المعدوم مسلوب عنه كل صفة وقيد بالثبوتية إذ يتصف المعدوم بالصفات العدمية فإنه في الحقيقة سلب الاتصاف بالصفات الثبوتية، قيل : هذا البيان إنما يدل على الاستلزام دون الفرعية ،والتوقف فالحق أن ثبوت شيء لشيء يستلزم ثبوت المثبت له في طرف الثبوت وحينئذ لا إشكال في قيام الوجود بالماهية والاتصاف به، وعندي أن الانصاف نسبة بين الطرفين فيحتاج إلى ثبوتهما فيه فيكون الاتصاف متوقفاً وفرعاً لثبوت المثبت له، فإن قيل : فيلزم أن يكون فرع ثبوت المثبت أيضاً ، قلت : نعم إذا كان الاتصاف حقيقياً كالاتصاف بالأعراض كما نص عليه الشيخ حيث قال في إلهيات الشفاء : إن ما لا يكون موجوداً في نفسه، استحال أن يكون موجداً لشيء، وأما إذا كان الاتصاف انتزاعياً كاتصاف زيد بالعمى، فلا يقتضي إلا ثبوت المثبت له لأنه لا بد من مبدأ الانتزاع في طرف الاتصاف حتى ينتزع منه.
The second aspect: The subsistence of a positive attribute in a thing is a branch of its existence—i.e., the existence of that thing in itself necessarily. For that which has no subsistence in itself cannot be qualified by a positive attribute, and there is no doubt that existence is a positive thing. So if existence were a superadded attribute [؟]. His statement: 'The second aspect, etc.' Its explanation: If existence were superadded to some quiddity, it would subsist in it; if it subsists in it, it would be a branch of its existence in itself; if it is a branch of its existence in itself, the quiddity would have an existence before its existence. The conclusion: If existence were superadded to the quiddity, the quiddity would have an existence before its existence, and the consequent is false, because it would necessitate the thing being existent twice, and the priority of existence over itself, or infinite regress. So the antecedent is false, thus it is established that existence is not superadded in any quiddity. His statement: 'For that which has no subsistence, etc.' The non-existent is stripped of every attribute, and he restricted it to positive attributes because the non-existent is qualified by privative attributes, for that is actually a negation of qualification by positive attributes. It is said: This demonstration only indicates the implication, not the branch-status and dependence. The truth is that the subsistence of a thing for a thing necessitates the subsistence of the subject of attribution in the realm of subsistence, and then there is no problem in the subsistence of existence in the quiddity and being qualified by it. In my view, attribution is a relation between two sides, so it needs their subsistence in it; thus the qualification is dependent and a branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution. If it is said: Then it would be a branch of the subsistence of the subject of attribution as well. I say: Yes, if the attribution is real, like the attribution of accidents, as the Master stated in the Ilāhiyyāt of al-Shifā': 'That which is not existent in itself cannot be the cause of something.' But if the attribution is abstractive, like the attribution of Zayd with blindness, it only requires the subsistence of the subject of attribution, because there must be a principle of abstraction in the side of the attribute from which it is abstracted.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof that existence cannot be a superadded attribute to quiddity. The argument is: A positive attribute (like existence) can only subsist in something that already exists in itself. If existence were a superadded attribute, it would have to subsist in the quiddity. But for it to subsist in the quiddity, the quiddity must already have existence in itself (since the subject of a positive attribute must be existent). This leads to a vicious regress or circularity: the quiddity would need an existence before its own existence. Therefore, existence cannot be superadded; it must be identical to or part of the quiddity. The commentary then discusses a subtlety: the argument might only prove that the quiddity must exist in some respect (thubūt) for the attribute to subsist, not necessarily that it has existence in the same sense. The commentator distinguishes between real attribution (like accidents) where the subject must be existent, and abstractive attribution (like blindness) where only the subject's subsistence in the mind is needed. However, in the case of existence, the attribution is real, so the quiddity must exist in itself before receiving existence as an attribute, which is impossible.

Key Terms
اتصاف حقيقي
اتصاف انتزاعي
ثبوت
مبدأ الانتزاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The second proof denies all accidental attributes because they also require an existent subject.
Correction: The proof only applies to real attributes like existence; abstractive attributes (e.g., blindness) do not require the subject to be existent in re, only in the mind.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what distinguishes real attribution from abstractive attribution?
A) Real attribution requires the subject to be non-existent
B) Real attribution requires the subject to exist in reality, while abstractive attribution only requires mental subsistence
C) Real attribution is only for divine attributes
D) Abstractive attribution requires the attribute to be real

Key Takeaway
The distinction between real and abstractive attribution saves the second proof by showing it only concerns real attributes like existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are the attributes you claim to have—like patience, generosity, or piety—real attributes that actually exist in your soul, or are they merely abstractive labels you apply to yourself while your actions contradict them? This lesson forces you to examine: what is truly attributed to you in reality? Commit to identifying one attribute you have been claiming abstractively and take a concrete step to make it real.
?
When you say 'I am a believer', is that a real attribution? Does your faith truly exist in your heart, or is it an abstractive label you wear without substance? The commentator shows that abstractive attributes only require a subject in the mind—they do not require the attribute to exist in reality. Ask yourself: is your faith a real, existential quality that governs your life, or is it just a name? What will you change to ensure your faith is real?
?
The lesson uses blindness as an example of an abstractive, privative attribute. Consider a privative attribute you might have, such as ignorance of a religious duty. If you remain ignorant after having the ability to learn, is that ignorance merely a privation or has it become a real attribute of negligence? This passage challenges you: what privative attributes are you allowing to define you? What will you actively do to replace them with positive, real attributes?

The Identity of Existence and Essence: A Reductio Proof
Al-Iji presents a reductio argument that superadded existence leads to three absurdities, proving existence identical to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Iji uses reductio ad absurdum to prove that existence cannot be a superadded attribute of essence, but is identical to it.

Core Idea
Existence cannot be added to essence without absurdity; it must be one with it.

Al-Iji presents a powerful argument that existence is not a separate attribute added to essence. If it were, we would face impossible consequences: the thing would exist twice, precede itself, or lead to an infinite regress. Since these are absurd, existence must be identical to essence. This passage demonstrates the use of logical reasoning in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Try to grasp the overall flow of the argument without getting bogged down in details.
The passage is a single continuous argument, so read it as a whole.
2
Identify the initial assumption
The argument begins by assuming that existence is an attribute that subsists in the essence (a superadded attribute). This assumption is the starting point for the reductio.
3
Trace the three absurd consequences
From the assumption, three absurdities follow: (1) the thing would exist twice, (2) self-precedence if the prior existence is identical, (3) infinite regress if the prior existence is different. Identify each in the text.
These are the core of the proof. Note how each is derived.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since all three possibilities are impossible, the original assumption must be false. Therefore, existence is not superadded but identical to essence. This is the desired conclusion.
The argument concludes that there must be an existence that is not preceded by another existence, which is the essence itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قائمة بالماهية لزم أن يكون قبل قيام الوجود بها لها وجود فيلزم كون الشيء موجوداً مرتين هذا خلف وأيضاً يلزم تقدم الشيء على نفسه إن كان الوجود السابق عين الوجود اللاحق ويعود الكلام في ذلك الوجود السابق إن كان غير الوجود اللاحق بأن يقال لو كان الوجود السابق صفة قائمة بالماهية لكان لها قبل قيام هذا الوجود بها وجود ثالث وتتسلسل الوجودات إلى ما لا نهاية له وهو ممتنع ومع امتناعه فلا بد هناك من وجود لا يكون بينه وبين الماهية وجود آخر قطعاً فيكون هو عين الماهية وذلك لأن جميع هذه الوجودات الزائدة التي لا تتناهى عارضة للماهية فتقتضي أن يكون لها وجود قبلها لامتناع اتصاف المعدوم بالصفات الثبوتية وذلك الوجود لا يكون زائداً على الماهية وإلا لم يكن ما فرضناه جميعاً جميعاً بل يكون عينها وهو المطلوب
If (existence) is an attribute subsisting in the essence, then it would be necessary that before the subsistence of existence in it, there be for it existence. So it follows that the thing exists twice; this is a contradiction. And also there follows self-precedence if the prior existence is identical to the subsequent existence. And the discussion returns to that prior existence if it is different from the subsequent existence, such that it is said: if the prior existence is an attribute subsisting in the essence, then there would be for it before the subsistence of this existence a third existence, and the existences would regress infinitely, which is impossible. And given its impossibility, there must be an existence between which and the essence there is no other existence, absolutely. Then it is identical to the essence. That is because all these superadded existences that are infinite in act are accidents to the essence, so they require that it have existence before them due to the impossibility of a non-existent being described by positive attributes. And that existence is not superadded to the essence, otherwise what we hypothesized would not be a totality; rather it is identical to it, which is what was sought.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage presents a proof by reductio ad absurdum (burhān khulf) that existence cannot be a superadded attribute of essence. The argument begins by supposing that existence is an attribute subsisting in the essence. If so, the essence must already have existence before that attribute attaches, otherwise how could it receive the attribute? This leads to the essence existing twice, which is absurd. Next, if the prior existence is identical to the later existence, then the thing precedes itself, which is absurd. If the prior existence is different, then we ask about that prior existence: if it is also an attribute, then it requires a further prior existence, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. Since all three possibilities are impossible, the original supposition is false. Therefore, there must be an existence that is not preceded by another existence; that existence is not superadded but is identical to the essence. The proof concludes that existence is identical to essence (al-wujud 'ayn al-mahiyya).

Key Terms
الوجود (al-wujud)
الماهية (al-mahiyya)
التسلسل (al-tasalsul)
الخلف (al-khulf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is about proving the existence of God.
Correction: The argument is about the relationship between existence and essence in contingent beings, not about proving God's existence. It assumes existence as an attribute and shows the absurdity of that view.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what follows if existence is an attribute superadded to essence?
A) The essence must be non-existent
B) The thing would exist twice
C) The essence would be eternal
D) Existence would be separate

Key Takeaway
Existence and essence are not distinct; existence is the very reality of the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your existence is not a mere label added to who you are but is your very essence, then why do you ever live as though your being is something you can separate from your actions? In what specific area of your life will you today align your actions with the truth that you are your being before God?
?
The argument relentlessly strips away every veil of separation between existence and essence. What 'existence' do you artificially add to your identity—status, possessions, roles—that you treat as separate from your true self? Confess one such attachment and decide how you will let it go.
?
Al-Iji’s reductio shows that any attempt to add existence to essence ends in infinite regress. Where in your spiritual life are you chasing an infinite regress of 'more'—more deeds, more knowledge, more experiences—as if your real existence is lacking? What would it mean to accept that your existence is already complete in God’s creative act, and how will you rest in that today?

Why Existence is Not an Attribute Existing Externally
Qurashi corrects the claim that necessary judgment requires existence as an external attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why existence is not an attribute existing externally, and why the necessary judgment about positive attributes does not apply to existence.

Core Idea
Existence is a mental distinction, not an external attribute.

In this passage, the author corrects a common mistake: applying general rules of certain intellectual judgments to existence itself. He argues that while positive attributes require external existence, existence itself is not such an attribute—it is distinct only in the mind. This clarification is crucial for understanding the nature of existence in relation to essence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correction
The author begins by rejecting a mistaken approach that applies general principles of conjectural sciences to certain intellectual judgments. Read the first few lines to see the correction.
The phrase 'فلايصح قطعا' indicates a strong rejection.
2
Understand the necessary judgment
The passage states that necessity judges that every positive attribute existing externally requires the subject's external existence. Grasp this conditional.
3
Distinguish existence from other attributes
Existence is not an external attribute; its distinctness from its substrate is only mental. Note the key term 'الامتياز الذهني'.
This is the core point.
4
Clarify 'positive'
Existence is called positive only in the sense that negation is not part of its concept, not because it exists externally. This prevents it from falling under the necessary judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : أن الوجود نفس الماهية أو جزؤها
للأحكام العقلية اليقينية بسبب ما يعارضها كما هو دأب أصحاب العلوم الظنية في أحكامها العامة فلايصح قطعا بل الصواب أن يقال : الضرورة تحكم بأن كل صفة ثبوتية أي موجودة في الخارج فإن قيامها بالموصوف فرع وجوده فيه، وليس الوجود صفة موجودة في الخارج بل امتيازه عن معروضه إنما هو في العقل وحده، نعم هو ثبوتي بمعنى أنه ليس السلب داخلا في مفهومه لا بمعنى أنه موجود في الخارج، فلا يكون مندرجاً في ذلك الحكم الضروري
The First Observation - The Third Purpose: That existence is the essence itself or a part of it.
For certain intellectual judgments, because of what opposes them, as is the habit of the practitioners of conjectural sciences in their general judgments, so it is absolutely not correct. Rather, the correct thing to say is: Necessity judges that every positive attribute, i.e., existing in the external, its inherence in the subject is a branch of its existence therein, and existence is not an attribute existing in the external; rather its distinctness from its substrate is only in the intellect alone. Yes, it is positive in the sense that negation is not included in its concept, not in the sense that it exists in the external, so it does not fall under that necessary judgment.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage begins with the heading of the section: 'The First Observation - The Third Purpose: That existence is the essence itself or a part of it.' The author then corrects a mistaken understanding about certain intellectual judgments. He argues that it is not valid to apply general principles from conjectural sciences to certain intellectual judgments because of opposing considerations. Instead, the correct position is that necessity (al-ḍarūra) judges that every positive attribute (ṣifa thubūtiyya) that exists externally (mawjūda fī al-khārij) requires the subject to exist in the external as a precondition for the attribute's inherence. However, existence (al-wujūd) itself is not an attribute existing externally; rather, its distinctness (imtiyāz) from its substrate (maʿrūḍ) occurs only in the intellect (al-ʿaql). Nevertheless, existence is positive (thubūtī) in the sense that negation is not part of its concept, not in the sense that it exists externally. Therefore, it does not fall under that necessary judgment. The passage thus clarifies that the necessary judgment about attributes requiring external existence does not apply to existence itself, which is a mental distinction.

Key Terms
الصفة الثبوتية
الوجود
الامتياز الذهني
الحكم الضروري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that existence is an attribute like whiteness that exists externally, and thus it falls under the necessary judgment that every positive attribute exists externally and its inherence requires the subject's external existence.
Correction: Existence is not an external attribute; its distinctness from its substrate is only mental. It is positive only in the sense that negation is not part of its concept, so it does not fall under that necessary judgment.

Checkpoint

B) Because existence is distinct from its substrate only in the intellect, not as an external attribute.
C) Because the necessary judgment is only for conjectural sciences.
D) Because existence is not a property of the subject.

Key Takeaway
Existence is a mental distinction, not an external attribute, so it does not fall under the necessary judgment that applies to attributes that exist externally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Objection that Essence Requires a Cause and the Answer
Debate on whether existence is identical to essence or additional, with objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the priority of cause over effect can be essential rather than existential, and how the addition of existence to essence can be interpreted mentally to avoid contradiction in the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Priority need not be existential; essential priority suffices to answer the objection.

In this passage, the author presents a common objection against the view that existence is additional to essence: if existence is additional, then essence requires a cause for that existence. The answer reveals a crucial distinction between existential and essential priority, and further refines the discussion by considering whether the addition is external or merely mental.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the objection is stated briefly, then the answer introduces a key distinction.
2
Identify the objection and the answer
The objection says that if existence is additional, essence needs a cause. The answer denies that priority must be existential.
The core move is distinguishing existential priority from essential priority.
3
Understand the refinement
The passage then clarifies that the addition might be external (in reality) or mental (in the mind). If mental, the need for a cause is only mental and not problematic.
This preserves the possibility that existence is additional in a certain sense without implying an external cause.
4
Recognize the identity view
The passage ends by noting that the proponent of identity claims unity of existence and essence in reality, which is a different position.
This final note shows the subtlety of the debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : أن الوجود نفس الماهية أو جزؤها
الماهية بها لا بد له من علة هي إما الماهية أو غيرها ) وأجيب عنه بأن العلة ) لا شك أنها ( متقدمة ) على المعلول ( وأما ) أن تقدمها عليه يجب أن يكون بالوجود فممنوع فإن التقدم الثابت للعلة بالقياس إلى المعلول (قد يكون بغير الوجود كتقدم الماهية عن حصول الوجود للماهية فهو وجود رابطي للوجود وليس ذلك واجباً، ولا ممتنعاً بل ممكناً فيحتاج إلى علة هذا ماقالوا في تنقيح هذا المقام وفيه بحث، لأنه إنما يتم إذا كان القائل بزيادته في الواجب قائلاً بزيادته في الخارج، وأن الاتصاف به حقيقي وأما إذا كان قائلاً بزيادته في الذهن بحسب نفس الأمر بمعنى أنه في حد ذاته بحيث إذا حصل في الذهن انتزع منه الوجود أمراً زائداً، على حقيقته فاللازم ليس إلا احتياجه إلى علة في هذا الانتزاع ولا محذور في ذلك فإنه محتاج فيه إلى الذهن أيضاً، وليس هذا اعترافاً بعينية الوجود في الواجب لأن القائل بالعينية يقول : باتحاد الوجود والماهية في نفس الأمر وعدم تغايرهما بالحقيقة فتدبر فإنه دقيق .
First observation - Third objective: That existence is identical to essence or a part of it. The essence necessarily has a cause that is either the essence or something else. And it was answered that the cause is undoubtedly prior to the effect. But that its priority over it must be by existence is denied. For the priority established for the cause in relation to the effect may be other than existence, like the priority of the essence over the occurrence of existence to the essence, so it is a relational existence to existence, and that is not necessary, nor impossible, but possible, so it needs a cause. This is what they said in refining this position, and in it there is discussion, because it is only valid if the one who says it is additional in the Necessary says it is additional externally, and that the attribute is real. But if he says it is additional in the mind according to the reality in itself, meaning that in its essence, when it occurs in the mind, existence is abstracted from it as an additional thing over its reality, then the necessary is only its need for a cause in this abstraction, and there is no harm in that, for it needs the mind also. And this is not an acknowledgment of the identity of existence in the Necessary, because the proponent of identity says: by the unity of existence and essence in reality and the absence of their true distinctness. So ponder, for it is subtle.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer regarding the relationship between existence and essence in the Necessary Being. The objection states that essence requires a cause, either itself or something else. The answer is that while the cause is prior to the effect, this priority does not have to be existential; it can be essential, such as the priority of essence over the occurrence of its existence. The passage then refines the discussion by distinguishing between those who hold that existence is additional to the essence externally versus mentally. If the addition is mental, then the need is only for a cause in the mind's abstraction, which is not problematic. The proponent of identity is noted as asserting the unity of existence and essence in reality. The passage ends by urging careful reflection due to its subtlety.

Types of Cause and Existential Priority
Explanation of cause types and essential entailment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between efficient causes (existentially prior) and essential entailment (prior by essence), and why not all causes require existential priority.

Core Idea
A cause can be prior by essence, not always by existence.

In this passage, the commentator responds to an objection about causality. He denies the universal claim that every cause must be existentially prior to its effect. Instead, he introduces different types of cause and explains that Allah's essence is a cause for His existence through entailment, not temporal priority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a denial followed by distinctions.
Pay attention to the types of cause mentioned.
2
Identify the three types of cause
The passage mentions efficient cause, receptive cause, and parts of essence. Distinguish them and note their characteristics.
The efficient cause is linked to temporal origination.
3
Understand the denial of existential priority
The commentator denies that every cause must be prior in existence. Grasp the nuance: some causes are prior by essence only.
This is key to understanding Allah's attributes.
4
Analyze the analogy of essence and determination
The example of an essence necessitating its determination shows how a cause can be prior only by essence.
This analogy illustrates essential entailment.
5
Connect to the broader theological context
Reflect on why this distinction matters for discussions of divine attributes and causality.
It prevents mistaken assumptions about God's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وأجيب عنه بأن إلخ) منع لقوله : والعلة إلخ أي كل علة متقدمة بالوجود أي لا نسلم كليتهما سواء أريد بالعلة العلة الفاعلية أو مطلق العلة مستنداً بالعلة القابلة وأجزاء الماهية. المؤثر هي متصفاً بالحدوث، نعم ماهيته تعالى علة لوجوده بمعنى : كونها مستلزمة ومقتضية له، لكن مستلزم الشيء ومقتضيه لا يجب أن يكون مقدماً عليه بالوجود، وهذا كما يحكمون بوقوع أن تقتضي ماهية تعيناً، فتكون منحصرة في فرد ولا شك أن تلك الماهية ليست متقدمة على تعينها بالوجود بل بالذات فقط، وأنت خبير بأن كون الحدوث علة الاحتياج إنما هو في غير الصفات كما صرح به في شرح المقاصد كيف ولو لم تستند الصفات الزائدة إلى الذات لزم تعدد الواجب، نعم فيه شائبة التخصيص من الأحكام العقلية كما لا يخفى،
His saying: 'And it was answered that...' is a denial of his saying: 'And the cause...', i.e., every cause is prior in existence, i.e., we do not accept its universality, whether by 'cause' is meant the efficient cause or absolute cause, relying on the receptive cause and the parts of the essence. The efficient cause is qualified by temporal origination. Yes, His essence, exalted, is a cause for His existence in the sense of being entailing and necessitating it. But that which entails a thing and necessitates it does not have to be prior to it in existence. This is like how they judge that an essence necessitates a determination, so it is confined to an individual, and there is no doubt that that essence is not prior to its determination in existence but only in essence. And you are aware that temporal origination being a cause of need is only in other than attributes, as clarified in Sharh al-Maqasid. How, if the additional attributes were not based on the essence, the multiplicity of the Necessary would follow. Yes, in it there is a shade of specification from rational judgments, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the previous objection and answer. It explains that the denial ('we do not accept') applies to the claim that every cause is prior in existence, whether efficient or absolute cause, including receptive cause and parts of essence. It then clarifies that the efficient cause is characterized by temporal origination, but the essence of the Necessary is a cause for His existence in the sense of entailment, not existential priority. An analogy is given: an essence can necessitate its own determination without existential priority. The commentator emphasizes that temporal origination as a cause of need applies only to contingent attributes, not to divine attributes, because otherwise multiple necessary beings would result. The passage ends by noting a subtlety of rational specification.

D) Essential cause

Key Takeaway
The distinction between existential priority and essential priority is crucial in understanding causality in divine attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The passage teaches that the divine essence entails existence without temporal precedence. How does this affect the way you view the permanence of God's attributes? Will you commit to deepening your study of His names to know Him more essentially?
?
If God is the cause of all things by essential entailment, then nothing exists outside His knowledge and power. What habits or sins do you entertain as if they are outside His presence? How will you change your thinking to live in constant awareness that He is the very ground of your existence?

Divine Attributes and the Cause of Need
Argument against temporal origination for divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why temporal origination cannot be the cause for divine attributes, and how this preserves the oneness of the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
If attributes were caused by temporal origination, multiplicity of the necessary would follow.

The commentator now applies the distinction between causes to the specific case of divine attributes. He argues that temporal origination is a cause of need only for contingent beings, not for Allah's attributes, because otherwise multiple necessary beings would result. This passage reinforces the doctrine of divine simplicity and the necessity of attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the source text and translation. This passage applies the earlier distinction to divine attributes.
Look for the phrase 'ḥudūth ‘illat al-iḥtiyāj'.
2
Identify the claim about temporal origination
The commentator states that temporal origination is a cause of need only for non-attributes, i.e., contingent beings.
This is supported by a reference to Sharh al-Maqāṣid.
3
Understand the consequence of attributing causality to attributes
If additional attributes were not grounded in the essence, multiplicity of the necessary would follow. Grasp the logical necessity.
This shows why attributes must be entailed by the essence.
4
Note the mention of rational specification
The passage ends with a remark about a shade of specification from rational judgments, indicating a subtle point.
This may refer to the fine-tuning of the argument.
5
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this passage defends divine simplicity and the necessity of attributes.
It strengthens the theological position against multiplicity.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the previous objection and answer. Why the Attribute of Existence Requires a Cause
Objection and rebuttal on necessity of existence attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attribution of existence to the Necessary is not necessary in itself and why it requires a cause.

Core Idea
Attribution itself is possible, even when what is attributed is necessary.

This passage presents a sophisticated kalam objection and its rebuttal. The objection argues that since the Necessary's existence is necessary, no cause is needed for its attribution. The rebuttal cleverly shifts focus: the attribution itself, as a relation between subject and predicate, is not necessary in itself but possible, thus requiring a cause to prefer its existence over non-existence. Let's follow the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation carefully. Notice the structure: objection, then rebuttal.
Pay attention to key terms like 'اتصاف' and 'علة ترجيح'.
2
Identify the objection
The objection claims that because the Necessary's existence is necessary, no cause is needed for its attribution. Ask yourself: what does the objection assume about attribution?
3
Understand the rebuttal's key move
The rebuttal argues that the attribution itself is not necessary in itself because it depends on a subject and predicate. Therefore, it is possible in itself and needs a cause to prefer its occurrence.
Note the distinction between the necessity of the object (existence) and the attribution relation.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this argument preserves the need for a cause while affirming the Necessary's existence. How does it avoid making the Necessary dependent?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال : اتصاف الشيء بأمر إذا كان ممكناً لم يكن بد من علة تجعل ذلك الشيء به واتصاف ذات الواجب تعالى بالوجود واجب فلا احتياج إلى العلة التي شأنها ترجيح أحد المتساويين على الآخر، نعم لو ثبت وجود وجوده الخاص لاحتاج إلى علة موجدة له وقد لا نسلم ذلك لجواز كونه من المعقولات الثانية كما قيل : لا بد لنفيه من دليل ورد بأن هذا إنما يتم إذا كان الاتصاف واجباً بالنظر إلى نفسه، وليس كذلك إذ ليس الاتصاف مما يتصور أن يستغني عما عداه بالكلية حتى يكون واجباً بالنظر إلى نفسه ضرورة احتياجه إلى موصوف وصفة فهو من حيث هو هو يكون إلا جائزاً، حصوله، ولا حصوله فلا بد من ترجيح أحد جانبي حصوله، ولا حصوله من مرجح إما الذات أو غيره ويلزم أحد المحذورين.
And it may be said: The attribution of a thing to an affair, if it is possible, must have a cause that makes that thing such. And the attribution of the essence of the Necessary, exalted, to existence is necessary, so there is no need for a cause whose function is to prefer one of two equals over the other. Yes, if the existence of His specific existence were established, it would need a cause that brings it into existence, and we may not accept that, because it may be among the secondary intelligibles. As it is said: It must be negated by a proof. It was replied that this is only valid if the attribution is necessary in itself, but it is not so, for attribution is not something that can dispense with others entirely so as to be necessary in itself, due to its need for a subject and a predicate. Thus, in itself, it is only possible, its occurrence and non-occurrence, so there must be a preference of one of its two sides of occurrence or non-occurrence from a preferrer, either the essence or another, and one of the two problems follows.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its rebuttal. The objection argues that the attribution of existence to the Necessary is necessary, so no cause is needed. The rebuttal replies that the attribution itself is not necessary in itself because it depends on a subject and predicate, making it possible, and thus requires a cause to prefer its existence over non-existence. The passage also considers that the specific existence may be a 'secondary intelligible' and therefore in need of a cause. The rebuttal emphasizes that the necessity of the attribution is only relative, not absolute.

The Receptive Cause and Parts Arguments
Author presents two arguments that priority is not by existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author argues that the priority of the receptive cause and the constitutive parts over essence is not by existence, thereby avoiding infinite regress.

Core Idea
Causal priority does not require existential priority.

In this passage, the author presents two arguments to show that priority can be established without assuming existence. He begins by pointing out that the possible essence is receptive to existence, and the receptive is prior to its recipient, but not by existence, as that would lead to absurdities. He then extends the same logic to the parts of essence, which are constitutive causes, and shows we can know their priority even when we disregard existence altogether.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the gist of the argument. Note how the author introduces the receptive cause and the parts argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two arguments
The first argument is about the receptive cause being prior but not by existence. The second is about the parts of essence being prior but not by existence. Notice the shared reasoning.
3
Understand why existential priority is rejected
He rejects existential priority because it would lead to a thing's existence before itself or an infinite regress. This shows that priority can be essential, not existential.
This connects to the broader doctrine that existence is not identical to essence.

First observation - Third objective: That existence is identical to essence or a part of it. The possible [essence] upon its existence, for it is receptive of existence according to you, and the receptive is prior to its recipient because it is a receptive cause for it. And that priority is not by existence, due to what you yourselves mentioned of the necessary occurrence of a thing's existence before its existence and its being twice existent, and the necessary occurrence of priority of a thing over itself or regress. And if the priority of the receptive is not by existence, then why may the priority of the agent not be likewise? And also, the parts are constitutive causes of the essence, and the constitutive of a thing is prior to it necessarily, because it is a cause for it. And that priority established for the parts is not by existence, for we are certain of that priority even if we disregard existence, i.e., the existence of the parts and the essence. For when we consider the essence in itself without considering existence or non-existence with it, we are certain of the priority of its parts over it. And if its priority were in terms of existence, that certainty would not be possible at all. Do not say: It, i.e., the priority of the constitutive over the essence, is also by existence, but not in terms of the actual occurrence of existence for both, but on the assumption of the occurrence of existence for both. For when we say 'the one is prior to the two,' we do not mean that both exist together and the one has priority in existence over the two, but we mean that they are such that when they exist, the existence of the part is prior to the existence of the whole. Therefore, this state, i.e., that the constitutive is such that when it exists together with what it constitutes, it is prior to it, is the priority established for the part in relation to the essence, and that it attaches to it, i.e., this state. His saying: 'And if...' is a verification that the receptive cause is a support for the denial, and in it there is an indication that what is meant is the efficient cause, because it is what the possible requires for its possibility. By his saying: 'so it has a cause,' i.e., 'high,' the commentator added, because the approach is not complete without considering causality, since the intention of the denier is that the cause does not have to be prior in existence, so it must be said that they are causes, and the intent is that their being constitutive causes is established among them and agreed upon. His saying: 'For when we consider the essence' i.e., the composite. His saying: 'we are certain of the priority of its parts' etc., i.e., that it needs the parts in the attainment of its essence. His saying: 'If its priority were in terms of existence, as in the efficient cause, receptive cause, final cause, conditions, and removal of impediments, then when we consider the essence in itself, we would not conceive any of it, let alone certainty of priority.' His saying: 'So this state is the priority because the result of the state is that the part is prior to the whole when both exist.' His saying: 'Receptive of existence according to you, in it there is discussion. For if it is meant that it is receptive of existence in the mind, then we do not accept that it is not prior by mental existence, necessarily, because the essence is realized in the mind first, then external existence is considered for it. And if it is meant that it is receptive of it in external [reality], then we do not accept that. It would only be receptive of it in external if the essence had another existence. Such is stated in al-Muhakamat, so ponder.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument spanning several moves. It begins by reasserting the topic: whether existence is identical to essence or a part. Then it presents an argument from the receptive cause: the essence is receptive of existence, and the receptive is prior to its recipient, but not by existence, to avoid circularity or regress. If the receptive cause can be prior non-existentially, then the agent cause can be as well. Then it presents an argument from parts: the parts are constitutive causes of the essence, and the constitutive is necessarily prior to the thing, but again not by existence, because we can be certain of this priority even if we disregard existence. The passage then anticipates an objection: that this priority is only on the assumption of existence, not in actual existence. The reply clarifies that the priority is in the state when both exist, not in actual existence. The rest is commentary explaining these points, including a discussion on whether the essence is receptive of existence in the mind or externally, and a reference to al-Muhakamat. The passage reinforces that existential priority is not necessary for causation, and that essential priority suffices.

Objection and Reply on Existential Priority of Parts
Objection and reply on the nature of parts' priority, with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that the priority of parts over the whole is only on the assumption of existence, and the author's reply that this priority is a state when both exist, not based on actual existence.

Core Idea
Priority of parts is a conditional state, not actual existential priority.

After establishing that parts are prior to essence without existential priority, an objector raises a subtle point: this priority is only if existence is assumed. The author responds by distinguishing between actual existential priority and a conditional state where the part's existence precedes the whole's when both exist. The commentary further discusses the nature of the receptive cause and the distinction between mental and external existence, inviting deeper reflection.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and reply
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. The objector says the priority is on the assumption of existence. The reply clarifies that this is a state, not actual existential priority.
Pay attention to the example of 'one is prior to two'.
2
Understand the reply's distinction
The reply distinguishes between actual existential priority (which is problematic) and a hypothetical state where the part's existence precedes the whole's when they exist together. This is a subtle but important distinction.
3
Explore the commentary
The commentary expands on the receptive cause, clarifying that it's really about efficient cause, and discusses whether the essence is receptive in mind or externally.
The commentary ends with 'ponder,' inviting the reader to reflect.

First observation - Third objective: That existence is identical to essence or a part of it. The possible [essence] upon its existence, for it is receptive of existence according to you, and the receptive is prior to its recipient because it is a receptive cause for it. And that priority is not by existence, due to what you yourselves mentioned of the necessary occurrence of a thing's existence before its existence and its being twice existent, and the necessary occurrence of priority of a thing over itself or regress. And if the priority of the receptive is not by existence, then why may the priority of the agent not be likewise? And also, the parts are constitutive causes of the essence, and the constitutive of a thing is prior to it necessarily, because it is a cause for it. And that priority established for the parts is not by existence, for we are certain of that priority even if we disregard existence, i.e., the existence of the parts and the essence. For when we consider the essence in itself without considering existence or non-existence with it, we are certain of the priority of its parts over it. And if its priority were in terms of existence, that certainty would not be possible at all. Do not say: It, i.e., the priority of the constitutive over the essence, is also by existence, but not in terms of the actual occurrence of existence for both, but on the assumption of the occurrence of existence for both. For when we say 'the one is prior to the two,' we do not mean that both exist together and the one has priority in existence over the two, but we mean that they are such that when they exist, the existence of the part is prior to the existence of the whole. Therefore, this state, i.e., that the constitutive is such that when it exists together with what it constitutes, it is prior to it, is the priority established for the part in relation to the essence, and that it attaches to it, i.e., this state. His saying: 'And if...' is a verification that the receptive cause is a support for the denial, and in it there is an indication that what is meant is the efficient cause, because it is what the possible requires for its possibility. By his saying: 'so it has a cause,' i.e., 'high,' the commentator added, because the approach is not complete without considering causality, since the intention of the denier is that the cause does not have to be prior in existence, so it must be said that they are causes, and the intent is that their being constitutive causes is established among them and agreed upon. His saying: 'For when we consider the essence' i.e., the composite. His saying: 'we are certain of the priority of its parts' etc., i.e., that it needs the parts in the attainment of its essence. His saying: 'If its priority were in terms of existence, as in the efficient cause, receptive cause, final cause, conditions, and removal of impediments, then when we consider the essence in itself, we would not conceive any of it, let alone certainty of priority.' His saying: 'So this state is the priority because the result of the state is that the part is prior to the whole when both exist.' His saying: 'Receptive of existence according to you, in it there is discussion. For if it is meant that it is receptive of existence in the mind, then we do not accept that it is not prior by mental existence, necessarily, because the essence is realized in the mind first, then external existence is considered for it. And if it is meant that it is receptive of it in external [reality], then we do not accept that. It would only be receptive of it in external if the essence had another existence. Such is stated in al-Muhakamat, so ponder.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument spanning several moves. It begins by reasserting the topic: whether existence is identical to essence or a part. Then it presents an argument from the receptive cause: the essence is receptive of existence, and the receptive is prior to its recipient, but not by existence, to avoid circularity or regress. If the receptive cause can be prior non-existentially, then the agent cause can be as well. Then it presents an argument from parts: the parts are constitutive causes of the essence, and the constitutive is necessarily prior to the thing, but again not by existence, because we can be certain of this priority even if we disregard existence. The passage then anticipates an objection: that this priority is only on the assumption of existence, not in actual existence. The reply clarifies that the priority is in the state when both exist, not in actual existence. The rest is commentary explaining these points, including a discussion on whether the essence is receptive of existence in the mind or externally, and a reference to al-Muhakamat. The passage reinforces that existential priority is not necessary for causation, and that essential priority suffices.

Misconception: One might think the objection invalidates the entire argument for essential priority.
Correction: The reply shows that the priority is a conditional state, not based on actual existence, so the argument stands.

Checkpoint

B) That it is only on the assumption of existence.
C) That it is impossible.
D) That it is based on God's will.

Key Takeaway
The priority of parts over the whole is a conditional state when both exist, not an actual existential priority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage discusses that the priority of parts is only on the assumption of existence. Are there beliefs about yourself (e.g., your 'parts' like status, achievements) that you treat as if they are existentially prior to your identity as a servant of God? How can you shift to seeing them as conditional states?

First Proof That Existence Is Additional to Essence in the Possible
Al-Jurjani states the first proof and its syllogistic explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof that existence is additional to essence in the possible, which uses a second-figure syllogism based on the possible essence's capacity for non-existence.

Core Idea
The possible essence's capacity for non-existence proves existence is not its essence.

This lesson presents the first of four arguments for the position that existence is additional to essence in possible beings. The argument uses a formal syllogism in the second figure to show that the possible essence, considered in itself, admits non-existence, while existence does not. This syllogism establishes a real distinction between essence and existence in contingent things.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage through once, then read the translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument from the initial statement to the commentator's clarification.
The passage includes both Al-Jurjani's text and the commentator's expansion.
2
Identify the two premises of the syllogism
Find the two premises the commentator gives: (1) the possible essence in itself admits non-existence, and (2) the possible essence taken with existence does not admit non-existence.
These are the core of the proof.
3
Understand the conclusion and its implication
The conclusion is that the essence is 'unlike the giver of existence to another.' This means existence is not part of the essence, because if it were, the essence could not admit non-existence.
4
Analyze the clarification about 'without regard to existence and non-existence'
The commentator clarifies that the constitutive cause is considered without regard to a specific existence or non-existence. Also note the incidental mention of non-existence.
This prevents a potential misunderstanding.
5
Consider the common misunderstanding
Some may think the proof is circular. Reflect on why this is not the case: the argument is based on the nature of possibility, not on an assumed conclusion.

المرصد الأول - المقصد الثالث : أن الوجود نفس الماهية أو جزؤها

وثالثها أنه زائد على الحقيقة في الواجب والممكن جميعاً فهاهنا بحثان: الأول أنه زائد على الماهية في الممكن لوجوه أربعة الأول أن الماهية الممكنة من حيث هي هي تقبل العدم. قال الشارح: قيل: هاتان المقدمتان أعني الماهية من حيث هي تقبل العدم والماهية المأخوذة مع الوجود لا تقبل العدم إذا انضمتا ينتج من الشكل الثاني أن الماهية بخلاف المفيد لوجود غيره، لأن بديهة العقل حاكمة بأنه ما لم يكن موجوداً لم يكن مفيداً لوجود الغير ومن هاهنا يستدل بالعالم على وجود الصانع تعالى. واعلم أن قوله بلا اعتبار وجود وعدم أي بلا اعتبار وجود بخصوصه وعدم بخصوصه فيصح قوله، وإلا لامتنع إلخ فإن قلت: يجوز أن يقومه باعتبار واحد من الأمرين الوجود والعدم فلا ينافي الجزم المذكور التردد في أحدهما قلت ذكر العدم استطرادي لأن التقويم إنما يتوهم باعتبار الوجود لا غير وهو المقصود بالمنع.
First Observation - Third Intention: That existence is identical to essence or a part of it. And third: That it is additional to reality in both the necessary and the possible. So here are two investigations: The first is that it is additional to essence in the possible for four reasons. The first: that the possible essence, in itself, admits non-existence. The commentator said: It is said: These two premises, namely the essence in itself admits non-existence, and the essence taken with existence does not admit non-existence, when combined, yield by the second figure that the essence is unlike the giver of existence to another, because the intuition of reason judges that as long as something does not exist, it cannot give existence to another, and from this we infer from the world the existence of the Creator, exalted. And know that his statement 'without regard to existence and non-existence' means without regard to a specific existence and a specific non-existence, so his statement is valid; otherwise it would be impossible etc. If you say: It is possible for it to constitute it by considering one of the two matters, existence or non-existence, then hesitation about one of them does not contradict the certainty mentioned. I say: Mentioning non-existence is incidental because constitution is only imagined by considering existence, nothing else, and that is the intended point of prohibition.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents the third opinion (that existence is additional to essence in both the necessary and the possible) and then gives the first of four proofs for the possible. The proof is: the possible essence in itself admits non-existence; if existence were identical to essence, it would not admit non-existence, because existence is the opposite of non-existence. The commentator explains this with a syllogism in the second figure (الشكل الثاني). The two premises are: (1) the possible essence in itself admits non-existence, and (2) the possible essence when taken with existence does not admit non-existence. The conclusion is that the essence is 'unlike the giver of existence to another' (بخلاف المفيد لوجود غيره), meaning that the essence does not give existence to itself, which implies that existence is not identical to essence. The commentator then clarifies a potential misunderstanding: when the author says the constitutive cause is considered 'without regard to existence and non-existence,' it means without regard to a specific existence or non-existence, not that both are equally considered. The mention of non-existence is incidental because constitution is only considered with respect to existence.

Key Terms
زائد (additional)
الماهية الممكنة (possible essence)
تقبل العدم (admits non-existence)
الشكل الثاني (second figure)
المفيد لوجود غيره (giver of existence to another)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular or assumes the conclusion that existence is additional.
Correction: The proof is a straightforward syllogism based on the nature of possibility: if existence were identical to essence, the essence could not admit non-existence because existence excludes non-existence. Thus, the proof does not assume the conclusion but derives it from the nature of possibility.

Checkpoint
What logical form is used in the commentary to prove that existence is additional to essence in the possible?
A) First figure syllogism
B) Second figure syllogism
C) Third figure syllogism
D) Analogical reasoning

Key Takeaway
The possible essence's indifference to existence and non-existence shows that existence is not part of its essence, thus existence is additional to essence in possible beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your existence is self-given, or do you acknowledge every moment that you could be nothing without the One who gives existence? What would change if you truly internalized that you, like all possible beings, are not the source of your own existence?
?
If you truly believed that your essence does not necessitate your existence, how would that affect your reliance on God? Would you feel more dependent, more grateful? Would you cling to Him more intensely?
?
The commentator notes this proof is also used to infer the Creator from the world. When you look at yourself, do you see evidence of your own contingency, or do you take your existence for granted? How could you cultivate a constant awareness of your need for the Giver of existence today?
